# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-mimir`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana-loki`

# Prometheus Alertmanager Notification Pipeline

## Your Task

Trace the alertmanager notification pipeline from a firing alert to the receiver dispatch in prometheus/alertmanager. Find Go source files implementing: alert ingestion, the routing tree traversal, the inhibition check, the silence check, and the final notifier dispatch.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

```json

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

49-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the analysis of the Prometheus Alertmanager notification pipeline. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Pipeline Flow

The alertmanager notification pipeline in Grafana Mimir follows this sequence:

1. **Alert Ingestion**: `Dispatcher.Run()` subscribes to alerts from the memory provider and processes them continuously

2. **Routing Tree Traversal**: `Route.Match()` performs a depth-first search through the routing configuration tree to find all matching routes for each alert

3. **Alert Processing**: `processAlert()` determines which aggregation group each alert belongs to and schedules notification dispatch

4. **Notification Pipeline**: The `PipelineBuilder.New()` creates a sequence of stages:
   - **GossipSettleStage** - Waits for cluster gossip to settle
   - **MuteStage (Inhibitor)** - Checks inhibition rules via `Inhibitor.Mutes()`
   - **TimeActiveStage** - Checks active time intervals
   - **TimeMuteStage** - Checks mute time intervals
   - **MuteStage (Silencer)** - Checks silence rules via `Silencer.Mutes()`
   - **Receiver stages** - Deduplication, retry, and dispatch

5. **Inhibition Check**: The `Inhibitor` maintains a cache of source alerts and checks if target alerts should be suppressed

6. **Silence Check**: The `Silencer` queries the silence store to check if alerts match active silences

7. **Final Dispatch**: `RetryStage.Exec()` sends notifications with exponential backoff retry logic

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, and a detailed explanation of the notification pipeline.

This can be simplified once the deprecated matcher syntax is removed.\n117: \tmatchers = append(matchers, cr.Matchers...)\n118: \n119: \tsort.Sort(matchers)\n120: \n121: \topts.MuteTimeIntervals = cr.MuteTimeIntervals\n122: \topts.ActiveTimeIntervals = cr.ActiveTimeIntervals\n123: \n124: \troute := &Route{\n125: \t\tparent:    parent,\n126: \t\tRouteOpts: opts,\n127: \t\tMatchers:  matchers,\n128: \t\tContinue:  cr.Continue,\n129: \t}\n130: \n131: \troute.Routes = NewRoutes(cr.Routes, route)\n132: \n133: \treturn route\n134: }\n135: \n136: // NewRoutes returns a slice of routes.\n137: func NewRoutes(croutes []*config.Route, parent *Route) []*Route {\n138: \tres := []*Route{}\n139: \tfor _, cr := range croutes {\n140: \t\tres = append(res, NewRoute(cr, parent))\n141: \t}\n142: \treturn res\n143: }\n144: \n145: // Match does a depth-first left-to-right search through the route tree\n146: // and returns the matching routing nodes.\n147: func (r *Route) Match(lset model.LabelSet) []*Route {\n148: \tif !r.Matchers.Matches(lset) {\n149: \t\treturn nil\n150: \t}\n151: \n152: \tvar all []*Route\n153: \n154: \tfor _, cr := range r.Routes {\n155: \t\tmatches := cr.Match(lset)\n156: \n157: \t\tall = append(all, matches...)\n158: \n159: \t\tif matches != nil && !cr.Continue {\n160: \t\t\tbreak\n161: \t\t}\n162: \t}\n163: \n164: \t// If no child nodes were matches, the current node itself is a match.\n165: \tif len(all) == 0 {\n166: \t\tall = append(all, r)\n167: \t}\n168: \n169: \treturn all\n170: }\n171: \n172: // Key returns a key for the route. It does not uniquely identify the route in general.\n173: func (r *Route) Key() string {\n174: \tb := strings.Builder{}\n175: \n176: \tif r.parent != nil {\n177: \t\tb.WriteString(r.parent.Key())\n178: \t\tb.WriteRune('/')\n179: \t}\n180: \tb.WriteString(r.Matchers.String())\n181: \treturn b.String()\n182: }\n183: \n184: // ID returns a unique identifier for the route.\n185: func (r *Route) ID() string {\n186: \tb := strings.Builder{}\n187: \n188: \tif r.parent != nil {\n189: \t\tb.WriteString(r.parent.ID())\n190: \t\tb.WriteRune('/')\n191: \t}\n192: \t\t\t\tb.WriteString(strconv.Itoa(i))\n200: \t\t\t\tbreak\n201: \t\t\t}\n202: \t\t}\n203: \t}\n204: \n205: \treturn b.String()\n206: }\n207: \n208: // Walk traverses the route tree in depth-first order.\n209: func (r *Route) Walk(visit func(*Route)) {\n210: \tvisit(r)\n211: \tfor i := range r.Routes {\n212: \t\tr.Routes[i].Walk(visit)\n213: \t}\n214: }\n215: \n216: // RouteOpts holds various {\\n669: \\t// If we haven't notified about the alert group before, notify right away\\n670: \\t// unless we only have resolved alerts.\\n671: \\tif entry == nil {\\n672: \\t\\treturn len(firing) > 0, \\\"fire\\\"\\n673: \\t}\\n674: \\n675: \\tif !entry.IsFiringSubset(firing) {\\n676: \\t\\treturn true, \\\"fire subset\\\"\\n677: \\t}\\n678: \\n679: \\t// Notify about all alerts being has passed.\\n695: \\treturn entry.Timestamp.Before(n.now().Add(-repeat)), \\\"repeat\\\"\\n696: }\\n697: \\n698: // Exec implements the Stage interface.\\n699: func (n *DedupStage) Exec(ctx \\\"reason\\\", reason)\\n763: \\treturn ctx, alerts, nil\\n764: }\\n765: \\n766: // RetryStage notifies via passed integration with exponential backoff until it\\n767: // succeeds. ctx.Err()\n603: \t}\n604: \treturn ctx, alerts, nil\n605: }\n606: \n607: // DedupStage filters alerts.\n608: // Filtering happens based on a notification log.\n609: type DedupStage struct {\n610: \trs    ResolvedSender\n611: \tnflog NotificationLog\n612: \trecv  *nflogpb.Receiver\n613: \n614: \tnow  func() time.Time\n615: \thash func(*types.Alert) uint64\n616: }\n617: \n618: // NewDedupStage wraps a DedupStage that runs against the given notification log.\n619: func NewDedupStage(rs ResolvedSender, l NotificationLog, recv *nflogpb.Receiver) *DedupStage {\n620: \treturn &DedupStage{\n621: time.Now().UTC()\n631: }\n632: \n633: // Wrap a slice in a struct so we can store a pointer in sync.Pool.\n634: type hashBuffer struct {\n635: \tbuf []byte\n636: }\n637: \n638: var hashBuffers = sync.Pool{\n639: \tNew: func() interface{} { return &hashBuffer{buf: make([]byte, 0, 1024)} },\n640: }\n641: \n642: func hashAlert(a *types.Alert) uint64 {\n643: \tconst sep = '\\xff'\n644: \n645: \thb := hashBuffers.Get().(*hashBuffer)\n646: \tdefer hashBuffers.Put(hb)\n647: \tb := hb.buf[:0]\n648: \n649: \tnames := make(model.LabelNames, 0, len(a.Labels))\n650: \n651: \tfor ln := range a.Labels {\n652: \t\tnames = append(names, ln)\n653: \t}\n654: \tsort.Sort(names)\n655: \n656: \tfor _, ln := range names {\n657: \t\tb = append(b, string(ln)...)\n658: \t\tb = append(b, sep)\n659: \t\tb = append(b, string(a.Labels[ln])...)\n660: \t\tb = append(b, sep)\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \thash := xxhash.Sum64(b)\n664: \n665: \treturn hash\n666: }\n667: \n668: func (n *DedupStage) needsUpdate(entry *nflogpb.Entry, firing, resolved map[uint64]struct{}, repeat time.Duration) (bool, string) {\n669: \t// If we haven't notified about the alert group before, notify right away\n670: \t// unless we only have resolved alerts.\n671: \tif entry == nil {\n672: \t\treturn len(firing) > 0, \"fire\"\n673: \t}\n674: \n675: \tif !entry.IsFiringSubset(firing) {\n676: \t\treturn true, \"fire subset\"\n677: \t}\n678: \n679: \t// Notify about all alerts being resolved.\n680: \t// This is done irrespective of the send_resolved flag to make sure that\n681: \t// the firing alerts are cleared from the notification log.\n682: \tif len(firing) == 0 {\n683: \t\t// If the current alert group and last notification contain no firing\n684: \t\t// alert, it means that some alerts have been fired and resolved during the\n685: \t\t// last interval. In this case, there is no need to notify the receiver\n686: \t\t// since it doesn't know about them.\n687: \t\treturn len(entry.FiringAlerts) > 0, \"resolve\"\n688: \t}\n689: \n690: \tif n.rs.SendResolved() && !entry.IsResolvedSubset(resolved) {\n691: \t\treturn true, \"resolve subset\"\n692: \t}\n693: \n694: \t// Nothing changed, only notify if the repeat interval has passed.\n695: \treturn entry.Timestamp.Before(n.now().Add(-repeat)), \"repeat\"\n696: }\n697: \n698: // Exec implements the Stage interface.\n699: func (n *DedupStage) Exec(ctx context.Context, l log.Logger, alerts ...*types.Alert) (context.Context, []*types.Alert, error) {\n700: \tgkey, ok := GroupKey(ctx)\n701: \tif !ok {\n702: \t\treturn ctx, nil, errors.New(\"group key missing\")\n703: \t}\n704: \n705: \trepeatInterval, ok := RepeatInterval(ctx)\n706: \tif !ok {\n707: \t\treturn ctx, nil, errors.New(\"repeat interval missing\")\n708: \t}\n709: \n710: \ttimeNow, ok := Now(ctx)\n711: \tif !ok {\n712: \t\treturn ctx, alerts, errors.New(\"missing now timestamp\")\n713: \t}\n714: \n715: \tfiringSet := map[uint64]struct{}{}\n716: \tresolvedSet := map[uint64]struct{}{}\n717: \tfiring := []uint64{}\n718: \tresolved := []uint64{}\n719: \n720: \tvar hash uint64\n721: \tfor _, a := range alerts {\n722: \t\thash = n.hash(a)\n723: \t\tif a.Resolved() {\n724: \t\t\tresolved = append(resolved, hash)\n725: \t\t\tresolvedSet[hash] = struct{}{}\n726: \t\t} else {\n727: \t\t\tfiring = append(firing, hash)\n728: \t\t\tfiringSet[hash] = struct{}{}\n729: \t\t}\n730: \t}\n731: \n732: \tctx = WithFiringAlerts(ctx, firing)\n733: \tctx = WithResolvedAlerts(ctx, resolved)\n734: \n735: \tentries, err := n.nflog.Query(nflog.QGroupKey(gkey), nflog.QReceiver(n.recv))\n736: \tif err != nil && !errors.Is(err, nflog.ErrNotFound) {\n737: \t\treturn ctx, nil, err\n738: \t}\n739: \n740: \tvar entry *nflogpb.Entry\n741: \tswitch len(entries) {\n742: \tcase 0:\n743: \tcase 1:\n744: \t\tentry = entries[0]\n745: \tdefault:\n746: \t\treturn ctx, nil, fmt.Errorf(\"unexpected entry result size %d\", len(entries))\n747: \t}\n748: \n749: \tneedsUpdate, reason := n.needsUpdate(entry, firingSet, resolvedSet, repeatInterval)\n750: \tif !needsUpdate {\n751: \t\treturn ctx, nil, nil\n752: \t}\n753: \t// now make sure that the current state is from past\n754: \tif entry != nil && entry.Timestamp.After(timeNow) {\n755: \t\tdiff := entry.Timestamp.Sub(timeNow)\n756: \t\t// when entry's timestamp is greater than the flushing time, it means that the pipeline was already ran by other Alertmanager instance while this one was sleeping in WaitStage.\n757: \t\t// In this case, this instance cannot proceed with the pipeline anymore because there is a risk that the instance holds the obsolete alerts, and it could cause flapping or duplicated notifications.\n758: \t\t// This could happen only in high-availability mode.\n759: \t\t_ = level.Warn(l).Log(\"msg\", \"Timestamp of notification log entry is after the current pipeline timestamp.\", \"entry_time\", entry.Timestamp, \"pipeline_time\", timeNow, \"diff\", diff, \"aggrGroup\", gkey, \"alerts\", fmt.Sprintf(\"%+v\", alerts), \"receiver\", n.recv.GroupName, \"integration\", n.recv.Integration, \"needsUpdateReason\", reason)\n760: \t\treturn ctx, nil, nil\n761: \t}\n762: \t_ = level.Debug(l).Log(\"msg\", \"Need to notify\", \"aggrGroup\", gkey, \"receiver\", n.recv.GroupName, \"integration\", n.recv.Integration, \"reason\", reason)\n763: \treturn ctx, alerts, nil\n764: }\n765: \n766: // RetryStage notifies via passed integration with exponential backoff until it\n767: // succeeds. It aborts if the context is canceled or timed out.\n768: type RetryStage struct {\n769: \tintegration *Integration\n770: \tgroupName   string\n771: \tmetrics     *Metrics\n772: \tlabelValues []string\n773: }\n774: \n775: // NewRetryStage returns a new instance of a RetryStage.\n776: func NewRetryStage(i *Integration, groupName string, metrics *Metrics) *RetryStage {\n777: \tlabelValues := \n806: func (r RetryStage) exec(ctx context.Context, l log.Logger, alerts ...*types.Alert) (context.Context, []*types.Alert, error) {\n807: \tvar sent []*types.Alert\n808: \n809: \t// If we shouldn't send notifications for resolved alerts, but there are only\n810: \t// resolved alerts, report them all as successfully notified (we still want the\n811: \t// notification log to log them for the next run of DedupStage).\n812: \tif !r.integration.SendResolved() {\n813: \t\tfiring, ok := FiringAlerts(ctx)\n814: \t\tif !ok {\n815: \t\t\treturn ctx, nil, errors.New(\"firing alerts missing\")\n816: \t\t}\n817: \t\tif len(firing) == 0 {\n818: \t\t\treturn ctx, alerts, nil\n819: \t\t}\n820: \t\tfor _, a := range alerts {\n821: \t\t\tif a.Status() != model.AlertResolved {\n822: \t\t\t\tsent = append(sent, a)\n823: \t\t\t}\n824: \t\t}\n825: \t} else {\n826: \t\tsent = alerts\n827: \t}\n828: \n829: \tb := backoff.NewExponentialBackOff()\n830: \tb.MaxElapsedTime = 0 // Always retry.\n831: \n832: \ttick := backoff.NewTicker(b)\n833: \tdefer tick.Stop()\n834: \n835: \tvar (\n836: \t\ti    = 0\n837: \t\tiErr error\n838: \t)\n839: \n840: \tl = log.With(l, \"receiver\", r.groupName, \"integration\", r.integration.String())\n841: \tif groupKey, ok := GroupKey(ctx); ok {\n842: \t\tl = log.With(l, \"aggrGroup\", groupKey)\n843: \t}\n844: \n845: \tfor {\n846: \t\ti++\n847: \t\t// Always check the context first to not notify again.\n848: \t\tselect {\n849: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n850: \t\t\tif iErr == nil {\n851: \t\t\t\tiErr = ctx.Err()\n852: \t\t\t\tif errors.Is(iErr, context.Canceled) {\n853: \t\t\t\t\tiErr = NewErrorWithReason(ContextCanceledReason, iErr)\n854: \t\t\t\t} else if errors.Is(iErr, context.DeadlineExceeded) {\n855: \t\t\t\t\tiErr = NewErrorWithReason(ContextDeadlineExceededReason, iErr)\n856: \t\t\t\t}\n857: \t\t\t}\n858: \n859: \t\t\tif iErr != nil {\n860: \t\t\t\treturn ctx, nil, fmt.Errorf(\"%s/%s: notify retry canceled after %d attempts: %w\", r.groupName, r.integration.String(), i, iErr)\n861: \t\t\t}\n862: \t\t\treturn ctx, nil, nil\n863: \t\tdefault:\n864: \t\t}\n865: \n866: \t\tselect {\n867: \t\tcase <-tick.C:\n868: \t\t\tnow := time.Now()\n869: \t\t\tretry, err := r.integration.Notify(ctx, sent...)\n870: \n871: \t\t\tduration := time.Since(now)\n872: \t\t\tr.metrics.notificationLatencySeconds.WithLabelValues(r.labelValues...).Observe(duration.Seconds())\n873: \t\t\tr.metrics.numNotificationRequestsTotal.WithLabelValues(r.labelValues...).Inc()\n874: \n875: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n876: \t\t\t\tr.metrics.numNotificationRequestsFailedTotal.WithLabelValues(r.labelValues...).Inc()\n877: \t\t\t\tif !retry {\n878: \t\t\t\t\treturn ctx, alerts, fmt.Errorf(\"%s/%s: notify retry canceled due to unrecoverable error after %d attempts: %w\", r.groupName, r.integration.String(), i, err)\n879: \t\t\t\t}\n880: \t\t\t\tif ctx.Err() == nil {\n881: \t\t\t\t\tif iErr == nil || err.Error() != iErr.Error() {\n882: \t\t\t\t\t\t// Log the error if the context isn't done and the error isn't the same as before.\n883: \t\t\t\t\t\tlevel.Warn(l).Log(\"msg\", \"Notify attempt failed, will retry later\", \"attempts\", i, \"err\", err)\n884: \t\t\t\t\t}\n885: \t\t\t\t\t// Save this error to be able to return the last seen error by an\n886: \t\t\t\t\t// integration upon context timeout.\n887: \t\t\t\t\tiErr = err\n888: \t\t\t\t}\n889: \t\t\t} else {\n890: \t\t\t\tlvl := level.Info(l)\n891: \t\t\t\tif i <= 1 {\n892: \t\t\t\t\tlvl = level.Debug(log.With(l, \"alerts\", fmt.Sprintf(\"%v\", alerts)))\n893: \t\t\t\t}\n894: \n895: \t\t\t\tlvl.Log(\"msg\", \"Notify success\", \"attempts\", i, \"duration\", duration)\n896: \t\t\t\treturn ctx, alerts, nil\n897: \t\t\t}\n898: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n899: \t\t\tif iErr == nil {\n900: \t\t\t\tiErr = ctx.Err()\n901: \t\t\t\tif errors.Is(iErr, context.Canceled) {\n902: \t\t\t\t\tiErr = NewErrorWithReason(ContextCanceledReason, iErr)\n903: \t\t\t\t} else if errors.Is(iErr, context.DeadlineExceeded) {\n904: \t\t\t\t\tiErr = NewErrorWithReason(ContextDeadlineExceededReason, iErr)\n905: \t\t\t\t}\n906: \t\t\t}\n907: \t\t\tif nil\n911: \t\t}\n912: \t}\n913: }\n914: \n915: // SetNotifiesStage sets the notification information about passed alerts. \n998: type TimeActiveStage timeStage\n999: \n1000: func NewTimeActiveStage(m types.TimeMuter, metrics *Metrics) *TimeActiveStage {\n1001: \treturn &TimeActiveStage{m, metrics}\n1002: }\n1003: \n1004: The Dispatcher.Run() method (line 147 in dispatch.go) initiates the pipeline by subscribing to incoming alerts via provider.AlertIterator. Source alerts matching SourceMatchers are cached, and target alerts matching TargetMatchers are checked against these cached source alerts. If both source and target matchers match and required labels are equal, the alert is inhibited.\\n\\n**6. Silence Check (silence/silence.go):**\\nThe Silencer.Mutes() method (line 113) queries the Silences store to check if the alert's labels match any active or pending silence matchers. It maintains a marker cache for efficiency, only doing full queries when new silences are added.\\n\\n**7. Final Notifier Dispatch (notify/notify.go):**\\nAfter passing all checks, the RetryStage.Exec() method (line 791) attempts to send notifications to the configured integration notifiers (email, slack, webhook, etc.) with exponential backoff retry logic.
